I composed this book for you, my sons, having completed it in its entirety as a part of the science of medicine. Having achieved clarity and explanation in it, I have seen fit to complete it for you with this chapter on manual surgery, which is a part of practice.
Indeed, the art of manual surgery in our land and time has become completely absent such that its science was nearly lost and forgotten. But there remain only a few rough sketches in the books of the ancients, obscured by hands and erased by errors and confusion such that their meanings are concealed and their usefulness is lost.
Therefore, I have seen fit to revive this art and compose this chapter on it with clear explanation, detailed description, and summary, and to include illustrations of surgical instruments and other tools used in practice.
The reason why there is no skilled craftsman of this art in our time is because the practice of medicine is lengthy, and its practitioner must first be proficient in the science of anatomy described by Galen. So that he may know the functions of organs, their structures, humors, connections and disconnections, the bones, nerves, muscles, their numbers and outlets, and the veins and arteries with their exits.
Therefore, as it is said, 'there are many physicians in name but few in deed,' especially in the art of manual surgery. We have mentioned this briefly at the beginning of this book.
For whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have mentioned regarding anatomy will surely fall into errors that kill people, as I have often witnessed many who claim to practice this art without knowledge or skill.
I once saw an ignorant doctor cut into a woman's neck to remove a swelling, damaging some of the vessels in her neck and causing her to bleed to death in his hands.
I saw another doctor who attempted to remove a large kidney stone from a man who had suffered abdominal stabbing, but in his haste he removed a piece of the bladder along with it. The man died three days later. When I was called to remove the stone, I saw its great size and understood how he had come to such a state.
I saw another doctor who earned his living among some lords of our land in medicine.
The doctor quickly, due to his ignorance, set the fracture on the wound near the heel using bandages and splints tied tightly without allowing any space for the wound to breathe.
Then he released him to his desires, left him for days, and ordered that the bandage not be loosened until his leg and foot swelled and approached ruin.
So I went to him and quickly untied the bandage, relieving his pain. But the corruption had already taken hold in the member, and I was unable to restore it.
Thus corruption spread throughout the limb until it perished.
I saw another doctor cauterize a cancerous tumor on someone's buttock. He performed the operation after several days until the patient's condition worsened, for if a cancer is purely from black bile, it should never be treated with iron.
Except when the entire member can be removed.
So know this, my son: work with the hand is divided into two categories - that which is accompanied by safety and that which is accompanied by harm in most cases.
And I have warned you throughout this book about operations that involve danger and fear, so you must avoid them and reject them.
So that the ignorant may not find an opportunity for speech and criticism. Therefore, be cautious and careful in your treatments, and gentle and steadfast with your patients.
And choose the safest and most preferable method leading to safety and favorable outcome. Avoid dangerous and difficult diseases that you cannot treat.
And keep yourselves away from what you fear may cause doubt in your religion and worldly life. It is better for you to leave it alone, as it raises your status in this life and the hereafter.
As Galen said in some of his advice: 'Do not treat evil diseases lest you become known as evil physicians.'
This section is divided into three chapters.
Chapter One.
Chapter One: Cauterization by Fire and Acid; arranged from head to foot, including images of instruments, descriptions of cautery irons, and everything needed for surgical operations.
The Second Chapter
On the Section on Cuts and the Abdomen, Bloodletting, Cupping, Surgeries, Extraction of Arrows and Similar Topics, All Categorized and Arranged with Illustrations of Instruments.
The Third Chapter
On the Section on Dislocations and Fractures, Treating Wounds and Similar Topics Categorized and Arranged from Head to Foot with Illustrations of Instruments.
The First Chapter
On Hemorrhoids
Before mentioning its use, it is necessary to mention its benefits and harms and in what constitution it is used.
I say that the discussion on the benefits and harms of Kîy is lengthy, subtle, precise knowledge, and many wise men have spoken about it.
And they differed in their opinions; I have summarized a little from what they said to avoid lengthening.
I say that Kîy generally benefits all bad constitutions, with or without matter, especially hot constitutions without matter and dry ones without matter.
As for dry constitutions with matter, they differed about it. Some said that Kîy is beneficial in it, while others said the opposite, that Kîy is not suitable in a disease resulting from heat and dryness because fire's nature is heat and dryness.
It is impossible to treat a hot, dry disease with a hot, dry remedy. The one who said the opposite claimed that Kîy can benefit a hot, dry disease occurring in people's bodies because of fire. For when you add moisture to fire, you make the body cold.
And I say that because I have experienced it many times, but it is not appropriate for anyone to think this way except those who are experienced and trained in the art of Kîy. And he stood on the variety of constitutions among people, the conditions of diseases within them, their causes, symptoms, and duration.
As for other constitutions, there is no fear of them for you, especially cold, moist diseases; all physicians agree on their benefit from Kîy and do not differ.
Know, O sons, that the secret of treating with Kîy by fire and its superiority over Kîy with a burned medicine is that fire is a simple substance whose effect does not extend beyond the part cauterized, and it scarcely harms any other connected part.
The application of burning drugs may extend its effect to nearby organs, and it might cause diseases in the member that are difficult to treat, or perhaps even cause death. Fire, due to its nobility and precious nature, does not do this unless one has been excessive.
And we have verified this through long experience in the practice of surgery and careful attention to the facts.
Therefore, I have omitted lengthy discourse; otherwise, it would not befit this book of mine to conceal from you the secret and mysterious nature of fire's action on bodies and its expulsion of diseases, lest I should perplex your understanding with philosophical arguments.
And know, O my sons, that physicians have disagreed about the appropriate time for cautery, and they considered the season of spring to be the most suitable time.
I say that cautery may be performed at any time because the harm caused by time is outweighed by the benefit derived from cautery. Especially if the cautery is for a severe, urgent and persistent pain that cannot be delayed, lest worse consequences follow than the slight harm caused by time.
And do not think, O my sons, as the common people and foolish physicians imagine, that cautery which cures a certain disease is a definitive cure without any recurrence.
For cautery is merely like a medicine that alters the temperament and dries up the humors that cause pain.
However, cautery surpasses medicine in its swift effect, powerful strength, and forceful control.
At times, the disease may return depending on the temperament of the patient, the severity of their condition, and the strength of their constitution, as well as factors such as their diet and other causes.
God forbid that cautery should be used for a light disease or in an organ of little importance and humidity. Such as the cauterization of a toothache, which may not return, especially if it is minor.
And the saying of the common people that cautery is the last resort of medicine is correct, not because they believe that no treatment will work after cautery has been performed.
And indeed, 'The Kye is the last resort of medicine' means that when we have used various remedies in treating an illness and they did not help, then we use the last resort of Kye and it works. Henceforth, Kye is considered the last resort of medicine. And not according to the meaning that has been understood by the common people and many ignorants among physicians.
It was mentioned by earlier authors that gold Kye is better than iron Kye. They said this because of the warmth and nobility of gold, claiming that it does not cause inflammation at the site of cauterization. This is not true.
Because I have tested it and found that it does not act equally on all bodies. Gold Kye is indeed better than iron, as they claimed, except that when you heat the cautery in fire made of gold, you cannot tell exactly when it reaches the desired temperature for its warmth.
Because it quickly cools down, and even if you increase its heat in the fire, it melts and the smith becomes confused by that. Therefore, iron Kye is quicker and more accurate for use, if God wills.
I have arranged this chapter on cautery into sections ordered from head to foot to make it easy for the student to find what he needs, if God wills.
Chapter One.
There is one type of Kye for the head.
This Kye is useful for excessive dampness and coldness in the brain, which are causes of headaches, frequent congestion in the head reaching to the eyes and ears, excessive sleep, toothache, and sore throat. In summary, it is used for all diseases caused by coldness such as paralysis, epilepsy, and shivering, etc.
The shape of this Kye is that you should first order the patient to evacuate using a purgative laxative suitable for the head, three or four nights in accordance with the patient's strength and age.
Then, order him to shave his head with a razor, then make him sit facing you while squatting, placing his hands on his chest.
Then place the base of your hand on the bridge of his nose between his eyes. Where your middle finger ends, mark that spot with ink.
Then heat the copper cautery that is of this shape.
Expose bone to the size of a chickpea or a grain of barley, then raise your hand and do not hesitate; prepare another spatula or use another one if it has cooled down. Until you see the bone as mentioned earlier, then take some salt, dissolve it in water, and soak a cotton pad in it. Place it on the location and leave it for three days.
Then place a cotton pad soaked in oil on it, leaving it until the crackling sound stops. Then treat it with the four-element plaster until it heals, God willing.
It has been said that the longer a wound remains open, the better and more beneficial it is for the pus to discharge.
Some have mentioned that they cauterize the skin until it reaches the bone and keep the cautery there until some of the thickness of the bone gets burned. Then they scrape off what has been burnt from the bone, after which they treat it.
Others have stated that one should exaggerate cauterization until it strongly affects the bone, causing a portion of the bone to collapse like a small ring or button. They claimed that this releases the headache's vapor from that location and leaves the wound open for an extended period.
Then treat it until it heals, but I do not find these two types of cauterization beneficial except in some cases. The safer option is to leave it alone; when the natural connection breaks, as we have seen in other parts of the body, inflammation occurs.
Especially if the patient's head is naturally weak; the first type of cauterization is the safest and best in my opinion, so use it and be safe, God willing.
Chapter Two.
On cauterizing the head.
If persistent headache occurs in the head, lasting for a long time without improvement despite using remedies, poultices, fumigations, ointments, and bandages – especially if cauterization with the single cautery described earlier did not help – then examine. If the patient's head is strong by nature and not weak, but feels extreme coldness, cauterize it with another cautery slightly above the first one. Then burn each corner of his head with a cautery until the skin thickens and the bone underneath is exposed, as described (before). Burn him with a cautery on the back of his head at the spot called the "nape" and be gentle in this, without exposing the bone, for he finds this cautery very painful unlike other head cauteries which I will mention later.
The cautery used for burning the corners of the head and the nape should be milder than that used for the middle of the head, and this is its shape.
Chapter Three.
Treating non-chronic headaches.
If pain occurs in a head wound accompanied by headache and the pain extends to the eye, evacuate the patient with diuretics for the head and use other treatments mentioned in the chapters on diseases. If this does not succeed, cauterize him on two sides (of the head). Either by cautery with a hot drug or with iron.
As for cauterization with the hot drug, take one garlic clove, peel it, cut off its ends on both sides, then make an incision on the painful side of the temple with a wide scalpel until a space is created under the skin sufficient to accommodate the garlic.
Insert it under the skin until it disappears, then tie it with a linen bandage and leave it for about fifteen hours. Then remove the garlic and allow the wound to heal for two or three days before dressing it.
Then dress it with cotton soaked in oil until the wound becomes inflamed, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if God wills. If you wish, you can do this with some of the cauterizing drugs mentioned in the eighteenth chapter on cauterizing drugs.
And as for cauterization with iron, it is done in this manner using an iron of this shape:
It is called the "mismariyya" cautery because its head is like a nail with some swelling and it has a small groove in its center.
Then place the cautery on the painful spot and hold your hand steady while you turn the iron slightly, burning to a depth equal to half the thickness of the skin. Raise your hand so that you do not burn the artery that is below, and thus cause bleeding. Then immerse a bandage in saltwater and apply it to the spot, leaving it for three days. Then remove the bandage with fat, then treat it with ointment until it heals, if Allah wills.
If you wish, cauterize this ulcer with the sharp end of a glowing coal from the fire, taking care not to cut the artery in this non-chronic ulcer.
Chapter Four.
In treating chronic ulcers.
If the treatment of ulcers that we have mentioned does not prove effective, and you see signs of the illness that are not covered by what has been mentioned regarding cauterization with fire or cauterization with medication. It is necessary to heat the pointed iron until it becomes white, then apply it on the spot of pain with a line about half a finger's length or similar, and leave your hand once while pulling it so that it cuts the artery and reaches close to the bone.
But you should be careful not to touch the movable jawbone while biting, so as not to burn its muscle or motor nerve and cause stiffness.
And beware of the bleeding from the artery that you cut, for in cutting it there is danger. Especially for those who are ignorant and have not practiced this craft, leaving the task to others.
And the method of treating sudden bleeding from an artery on the face will be mentioned in its place in this book, if Allah wills. If you see signs of the illness that are not covered by this cauterization.
And if you find the patient's body tolerating it, perform cautery in the middle of the head as described and treat the wound until it heals, if Allah wills.
If you wish, you can use the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on tying off an artery with a double-pointed iron; it is better and more effective than this one.
Chapter Five.
In treating earache.
If an earache occurs due to cold, and it is treated with laxatives and other treatments mentioned in this section but the pain persists, heat the iron called 'al-Nuktah' which has this shape.
Then prick it with this after heating around both ears entirely as it rotates, or around them all if the pain is in both. Then keep it a little away from the root of the ear after marking the spot with ink, and let the cautery be about ten points in each ear or thereabouts, then treat the spots until they heal, if Allah wills.
Chapter Six
In cauterization.
The phlegm that is treated by cautery is of the type that occurs as described in the sections on diseases.
And avoid cauterizing types that result from concavity and nerve spasm.
If you have treated this type of phlegm with remedies, syrups, and decoctions but found them ineffective, then it is permissible to cauterize the patient three times. Once at the root of the ear, second below it slightly near the cheekbone, and third at the meeting point of the lips.
Make your cautery on the opposite side of the affected area, for relaxation occurs only on the healthy side that appears sound.
The form of cautery should be two cauteries facing the tip of the upper ear slightly below the vertex of the head, and another on the cheekbone, each about the length of a finger joint.
Lower your hand with the cautery until you burn about half the thickness of the skin, and this is the form of the cautery, which is a type of spatula that was previously depicted, though it is somewhat smoother as shown. The spatula should have a blade slightly thicker than the rest, then treat the spot with what has been mentioned until it heals, if Allah wills.
Chapter Seven
In cauterizing chronic ulcers.
If the ulcer has become chronic and you have treated it with what was mentioned but found no effect, and there is no fever in the patient, then cauterize four times. Once on each temple, once at the crown of the head as mentioned earlier, and once at the back of the head as previously described.
And the recipe for cauterization as mentioned earlier; also, you can cauterize once on the stomach's mouth and apply more ointment, then treat with what has been mentioned.
Chapter Eight
In Forgetfulness
If it is due to phlegm, it is advisable that the patient first be given large quantities of diuretics and brain-purifying drugs.
Then his entire head should be shaved, and a poultice of mustard plaster written in the chapter on ulcers should be applied to it repeatedly, for this is one method of treating forgetfulness.
And do this on the precise spot mentioned earlier; for it will cure him, God willing. If not, then perform cupping three times at the back of his head from the top to below the neck.
And place between each cupping a finger's width apart, then treat the forgetfulness as previously mentioned. If you wish to increase it and the patient is able to tolerate it, perform an additional central cupping.
If you wish to increase [the treatment], then perform cupping on the ears also, and treat him until he is cured. The cups should be made of brass, as described previously.
Chapter Nine
In Paralysis and General Weakness of the Body
It is advisable to begin by purging the head with diuretics and other treatments mentioned earlier, then shave the patient's head and perform cupping once in the center of the head, once on each ear, and once at the back of the neck.
And three times on the nape of the neck. If you need to perform more cupping for a case of general weakness and the patient is able to tolerate it, and the illness is severe and well-established, then perform four cups on the backbone. Inform him about the cupping until it burns more of the skin, then lift your hand and treat him as previously mentioned until he is cured, God willing. The cups should be made of brass.
Chapter Ten
In Epilepsy
Only perform cupping on an epileptic whose seizures are due to phlegm. It is advisable to first purge his brain with large diuretics and other treatments mentioned earlier if the patient is able to tolerate taking drugs.
But if he is a child who cannot tolerate drugs, then use the brain-purging gruel and syrup for many days before cupping, along with improving his diet.
Then he shaves his head and applies the first cautery iron in the middle of the head as mentioned earlier, and another cautery iron at the back. And on each horn of his head, cautery irons are applied. If the patient is strong and can withstand it, cauterize them as mentioned in "The Paralytic". Relax the body over the cervical spine and thoracic vertebrae. The cautery iron should be oily as previously described.
If the patient is a child, make the cautery iron mild like this.
Chapter Eleven.
On Melancholia.
If the cause of melancholy is corrupt humors and thick phlegm, cauterize with the irons mentioned in "The Paralytic".
If the cause of melancholy is an inclination towards black bile and the patient's body is moist and corrupt, then cleanse his brain as previously mentioned in division.
Then shave the patient's head, make a tight cap of linen like a crown, and place it on his head while he is sitting cross-legged, holding it from all sides. Then take one spoonful of old sheep fat.
Heat it gently over the fire until it can be tolerated by touching with a finger, then pour it into the cap on his head and leave it until it cools. Repeat this process once every week along with other good treatments until he recovers, if Allah wills.
If you wish, cauterize him with many small punctures without holding the iron in your hand, but rather touching lightly. This type of cautery moistens the brain moderately.
Then apply to him a linen cloth soaked in sheep fat or chicken grease.
Chapter Twelve.
On Cauterization for Watery Eye Discharge.
If you find that watery eye discharge has begun with the signs mentioned in division, hurry to cleanse the patient's head and warm him up from all humidities. Wash him in the bathhouse on an empty stomach for several days.
Then shave his head, cauterize him with one iron in the middle of his head, and two irons on the temples if both eyes are affected. If only one eye is affected, cauterize on that side alone.
Then cut with the scalpel all veins and arteries that are under the skin, let the incisions be long in width of a fingerbreadth on both cheeks, and take care not to cause bleeding.
If you find any of it, then cut it off at the point with whatever treatment is available to you. We will come later to the wisdom in tying the vessels and cutting them while taking care not to cause bleeding.
You should make two incisions under the bone on either side of the spine.
Chapter Thirteen.
On Chronic Weeping.
If the tears from the eye are chronic and continuous, and it has been ascertained that this is due to cold humors rising from the brain through the veins and arteries on the surface of the head, then cauterize with the iron that I have described at the beginning of the descent of the water. Make an incision in the middle of the forehead, two incisions on either cheekbone, and two incisions under the bone at the nape of the neck. If more is needed, make additional incisions on each side of the eye's tail at the edge of the eyebrow using a small scalpel.
Chapter Fourteen
On Cauterization for Epistaxis
If the treatment mentioned in the section does not prove effective, then hasten to apply a plaster made of wax for three nights. Then shave his head and cauterize the middle vein on the forehead using an oil-soaked scalpel. Then cauterize with the red-hot iron two incisions above the eyebrows slightly beneath the hair, taking care not to cut the artery. Here is an illustration of the smaltery:
Chapter Fifteen
On Cauterization for Drooping Eyelid
If the eyelid droops due to disease or dampness, cauterize the eyelid with one incision using this crescent-shaped scalpel.
And if you wish, cauterize slightly above the eyebrows on both sides, two incisions each, keeping away from the cheeks. Let the length of each incision be equal to that of the eyebrow.
Do not exaggerate in cauterizing, let it only burn a third of the skin. The shape of the scalpel is like this:
Chapter Sixteenth
In eye cupping
If the eyelids turn inward causing entropion, then there are two kinds of eye cupping. Either by fire cautery or by drug cautery; as for cauterization with fire, the patient should beforehand stop pulling at his eyelashes if he does so that they may grow long and even.
When the lashes grow back and become steady, bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they have grown. When they have grown and become even, place the patient's head on your lap then mark with ink an outline resembling the shape of an almond leaf onto the eyelid.
Begin marking at the base of the lashes, then place beneath the eyelid a pad soaked in egg white or sparrow's saliva. Then heat an iron cautery with this shape.
Then cauterize according to the shape you have marked, a little at a time many times until the skin surface burns like the entire almond leaf shape. A sign of your success is when the eyelid has shrunken and the lashes have risen away from the eyeball.
Then raise your hand and leave him for three days. Then apply a bandage soaked in butter until the lashes fall out, then treat with ointment until it heals God willing. If any hair returns later and the eyelid relaxes again...
...repeat the cauterization as before. If there is hair on the lower eyelid, cauterize until it returns to its natural position and does not turn inward again. As for cautery with burnt drug...
Then make a paper shape resembling an almond leaf. Take equal weights of common soap and un-slaked lime, about one pound each, grind them together quickly without letting it dry. Then spread this mixture onto the paper shape you made, place it on the eyelid or both eyes, and put a pad soaked in egg white under the eye. Place the patient's head on your lap.
Place your index finger above the medication and press it slightly while moving it whenever the patient feels pain due to the sensation of the medicine being like fire. Continue until the sensation subsides, then remove the medication and wash the eye with water.
If you observe that the eyelid has risen as it does when burned by fire or cut, then apply more medication to the unaffected area until your task is complete and the eye is healed. Then place cotton soaked in oil onto it until the burning sensation subsides.
Then treat it with the yellow ointment or other similar remedies until it heals. When performing this procedure, be extremely careful not to let any medication fall into the eye, as if the eyelid relaxes after several days and some hair enters the eye.
So repeat applying the medication to that relaxed eyelid area, especially as you did initially. Then treat it until it heals, and this is the image of the date leaf.
Know that people's eyes differ in size from one another, so adjust your cautery accordingly. There is no fixed method for those who have experience in this craft.
Chapter Seventeen
The treatment of styes which appear at the corner of the eye.
If after treating a sty with what has been mentioned in the sections on diseases, it does not improve, then cauterize it as follows:
Order the patient to place their head in your lap and have a servant hold their head firmly between their hands so that it does not move or shake.
Then place a cotton pad soaked in egg white or spittle on the patient's eyes, and heat the cautery, which has this shape:
The cautery should be shaped like a hollow tube resembling the shape of an eagle's feather at one end, which is used for cauterization. If you wish, it can be open at the other end or closed like a reed, although this hollow tube is preferable for your work, if God wills.
Then squeeze the sty if it is open and remove its contents, or if it is not open, cut it open and extract its pus. Then place the heated cautery on it while holding it with your hand until it reaches the bone.
Move your hand slightly away from the eye towards the nose so that your hand does not err nor disturb the patient, lest the spatula fall upon the eye's membrane and spoil it. If you reach the first sinus of the bone, proceed; otherwise, prepare the spatula again if necessary.
Leave him for three days, then apply a linen cloth soaked in butter and treat him with dried ointment until he recovers. If forty days pass and he has not recovered, apply the sharp medicine that consumes until the bone is exposed, as mentioned later in its chapter, if God wills.
Another method for treating the nasal sinus, as mentioned by some early authors: approach the location of the sinus and make an incision there. Then place a thin funnel into the same cut; this is its appearance.
Pour into it about the weight of a dirham of melted lead and hold the funnel firmly with your hand, ensuring that the patient does not move so that the molten lead does not flow into their eye. It is preferable to place a wet cloth soaked in egg white or water over the patient's eye.
For the lead burns the location of the sinus and heals it with a wonderful healing. If the sinus is healed by what we have mentioned about the cure and treatment, otherwise, it is necessary to use nasal cautery and restore the sinus to its proper position in the nose, as will be discussed more specifically later on.
Chapter Eighteen.
On the Treatment of Cleft Lip.
A common occurrence is the cleft lip, known as "the hair," especially in children. If treatment of this cleft by what was mentioned earlier does not prove effective, then prepare a small, thin spatula shaped like this:
Make its hollow like the edge of a blade, then place it heated with embers into the same cleft until the cautery reaches the depth of the cleft. Then treat it with tartar ointment until it heals, if God wills.
Chapter Nineteen
On the Treatment of Nasal Sinus Located in the Mouth
If a swelling appears at the root of the teeth or in the gum or at the roots of the jaws, then it becomes inflamed and bursts open to become a nasal sinus from which pus flows. If treatment proves ineffective, then heat a spatula according to the size that fits into the sinus.
Then, introduce it through the hole of the nose, protecting it with gauze until you reach the depth required. Repeat this once or twice then treat it as mentioned earlier until it heals, if Allah wills.
If the matter is cut off and healed, then no incision is necessary; otherwise, it is mandatory to expose the site and remove the rotting bone as will be described later, if Allah wills.
Chapter Twenty.
On fractures of the jaws and loosened teeth.
If the gums have softened due to moisture and the teeth have become loose, despite treating them with medication without success, then place the head of the clamp in your palm and warm the bellows whose image is shown below by placing the tube on the tooth.
Then insert the bellows protected with tinder, holding your hand for a moment until the patient feels the heat of the fire has reached the root of the tooth. Then remove your hand and repeat this process as desired. Then the patient should rinse their mouth with saltwater.
He holds it for a moment then releases it; this will stabilize the loose tooth and firm up the relaxed gums, drying out the rotting moisture.
Chapter Twenty-One.
On toothache.
If the toothache is caused by cold or has decay, despite treating it with medication without success, then there are two options for treatment: either cauterization with butter or cauterization with fire.
As for cauterization with butter, you should take some cow's butter and melt it in an iron spoon or seashell. Then take a piece of cloth, dip it into the melted butter, wrap it around the tip of a probe, and apply it to the painful tooth with haste, holding it until it cools down.
Repeat this several times until the heat reaches the root of the tooth. Alternatively, you may dip a wick or cloth in cold butter and place it on the painful tooth while placing the heated iron above it until the fire reaches the bottom of the tooth.
As for cauterization with fire, you should use a copper or iron tube with some thickness to prevent the heat of the fire from reaching the patient's mouth. Then warm the bellows whose image is shown and place it on the same tooth while holding your hand until the bellows cools down. Repeat this several times.
If pain goes away either on that day or the following, then after that it is necessary to fill the patient's mouth with good clarified butter and hold him for a moment before expelling it. This is an image of the mold.
Mold can be done on whichever side you wish and at whatever size is possible, and this is an image of the funnel.
The Twenty-Second Chapter
Regarding the Molding of the Pig's Snout
If pigs are affected by phlegm and cold dampness, and do not improve with medications, and you want a quick improvement, then use the hollow mold whose image is shown here with both ends open.
To let smoke out at the other end of the mold, place it protectively on the same tumor once or twice if necessary until you reach the depth of the tumor. If the tumor is small, make the mold to fit its size.
Then leave it for three days, and apply a cloth dipped in clarified butter until what was burned by the fire goes away. Then treat it with ointment and bandages until it heals, if God wills.
The Twenty-Third Chapter
Regarding Molding for Hoarseness of Voice and Shortness of Breath
If phlegm has taken hold of the trachea, especially if accompanied by coldness of temperament, it is necessary for the patient to first use laxative medications, then apply a mold to the hollow of the neck at the base of the larynx.
Be careful not to reach the larynx with the mold, and do not burn more than a small amount of skin. Then apply another mold at the junction of the neck with the shoulder, making it conical according to the size mentioned.
Then treat him as mentioned earlier until he recovers, if God wills.
The Twenty-Fourth Chapter
Regarding Molding for Lung Disease and Cough
If cough and lung disease are due to cold phlegm, without fever or chills, and the disease is chronic, apply molds on both hollows of the shoulders at the lowest points, and another mold in the center of the chest between the breasts.
The cautery should be made of iron, as depicted. If you wish, it can also be made with the pointed cautery called 'the Dot', whose image has been shown in the treatment of earache. The dots should number approximately thirty.
Then treat it as mentioned earlier until it heals. You can also make a cautery with three prongs, as shown in the image; this will expedite the procedure as you can cauterize three vessels at once. This is an image of the cautery.
Chapter Twenty-Fifth
In cauterizing the buttocks.
If the head of the shoulder joint becomes dislocated due to slippery fluids or does not remain in place and has been repeatedly replaced until it has become a habit, then it should not be reduced again initially. Then the patient lies on their back or the affected side. Then lift the skin inside the buttocks upwards with fingers from your left hand if the joint has dislocated inwards.
Then heat the cautery with two prongs, as shown in this image.
Then cauterize the skin with it until it penetrates to the other side, making four incisions. Alternatively, you can use a cautery with three prongs, resulting in six incisions, with the prongs resting on the soft flesh.
This is an image of the cautery with three prongs.
Adding one more incision will result in eight incisions. Then apply the ground crusts with salt to the cautery. Keep the patient at rest and do not move the limb until it has healed. Dislocation upwards rarely occurs.
Cauterize above the shoulder joint once with a large iron cautery or perform multiple punctures to reduce the joint and eliminate moisture, leading to recovery.
Chapter Twenty-Sixth
On cauterizing the stomach
If there is coldness and excessive moisture in the stomach causing vomiting, frequent indigestion despite various treatments proving ineffective, then lie the patient on their back with legs and arms extended. Then cauterize three times. A triangle-shaped design is made under the breastbone with a lancet, and two below the knees. Each incision should be like this until the incisions resemble a triangle shape, keeping them apart so they do not merge upon healing. The depth of the incision should be about one-third the thickness of the skin.
As shown in this image and to this extent, no more.
If you wish, make a single large incision in the middle of the abdomen as shown in this image.
And the lancet used for this single incision should be circular-shaped as shown in this image.
Instead, the abdomen can be marked with dots for those who are hesitant about this incision. Using a pen, mark points on the abdomen to the desired depth, then use a puncturing lancet to make the incisions, and treat them according to the method mentioned until they heal.
Chapter Twenty-Seventh.
In cold liver incision.
If the patient suffers from pain in the liver due to coldness and dampness or wind excess, such that it exceeds its normal state, despite treatment with what has been mentioned previously without success. It is necessary for the patient to lie on their back and mark three incisions of this shape and size on the liver below the ribs where the human elbow ends.
And after each incision, make another incision equal to the thickness of a finger, with the incision running straight along the body without pressing too hard with the lancet.
And burn only half the thickness of the skin, no more. The patient should stand on their feet; if they cannot stand, then lie down with legs extended and arms raised. This is an image of the cautery.
And you may use the cautery lancet to burn these incisions if you are skilled and careful, being cautious not to burn too deeply as the skin there is thin, so as not to reach the intestines.
Chapter Twenty-Eighth.
In treating an enlarged liver by incision.
If a swelling appears on the liver and you wish to determine whether it is in the flesh of the liver or its capsule, if it is in the flesh of the liver, the patient will feel heavy and painful without definite limits.
If there is inflammation in the liver, causing severe pain, which has baffled physicians regarding its treatment, then have the patient lie on their back and apply a poultice at the warm spot with ink.
Then heat the iron in the fire, this being the one that resembles the letter 'mim', which is its shape. And apply it once, until all the skin is burned and the heat reaches the liver, allowing all the matter to come out. Then treat as you would a boil until it heals.
And this method of cautery should only be employed by one who has extensive training in the art of medicine and has practiced it many times, for I would prefer to leave such work to him.
Chapter Twenty-Nine
On Cauterizing a Hemorrhoid.
The ancients described cauterizing a prolapsed hemorrhoid using the roots of asafoetida thus: Take one long, dry root of asafoetida, as thick as a finger, dip it in oil, and heat it in fire. Then apply it once between the neck and the collarbone, two small cauteries near the ears slightly leaning towards the beard area, and two large cauteries above the chest between the third and fourth ribs.
And two more between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclined slightly towards the back, one in the middle of the chest, another above the stomach, three behind one another between the shoulders, and two on either side of the rib cage below the elbow cautery.
It is not necessary to press deeply with the cautery, but rather to use it lightly on the surface of the skin. Some authorities mention that some people use an iron cautery resembling the letter 'mim', heating it and inserting it between the buttocks until it reaches the actual prolapse.
And the matter will come out as mentioned in the case of liver prolapse. In this case, cauterizing the anus with a hot iron can either kill the patient immediately or leave them with sores that will not heal.
Chapter Thirty
Of the spleen.
If you have treated the spleen with what has been mentioned in the division of medicine, and your treatment did not prove effective, then cauterize it at three points, all of which are accurate: either three or four evenly spaced ones along the length of the spleen.
Shape them like the liver cauterizations that have been shown, with each cauterization being about the thickness of a finger or slightly more. The shape of the cautery should be as described for liver cauterization, without pressing too deeply. The patient should lie on their back during this procedure.
The second method is at the elbow joint. Raise the skin that faces the spleen where the patient's right elbow ends, and also raise the skin that faces the spleen where the left elbow ends. The raising of the skin should be across the width of the body so that the cauterizations are along the length of the body.
Then insert both needles carefully until they penetrate the skin on the other side. Remove the cautery, resulting in four cauterizations. If you wish, you can also use the three-pronged cautery.
Then treat the site of cauterization after allowing it to discharge pus for many days, as this is the most effective treatment among those mentioned before.
Chapter Thirty-One
Of Trepanation
Trepanation is beneficial only in cases of acute hydrocephalus, especially if other treatments mentioned in the division have not proven effective. In such case, cauterize four points around the scar and one point on the abdomen.
And another cauterization on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back between the shoulder blades, one near the chest and the other near the abdomen. The depth of the cauterizations should be close to the thickness of the skin. Then leave the wound open to discharge pus for a long time.
The patient should not be deprived of other treatments after cauterization, as combining them will hasten recovery. The shape of the cautery used for the back should be pointed, as previously described, and the one used for the abdomen should be spoon-shaped.
The Second and Thirtieth Chapter
In the Treatment of Feet and Legs
If swelling appears in the foot and it fills with yellow water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot at the furrow between the little toe and the ring toe.
And hold your hand steady with the cauterizer, do not move it, then raise your hand without returning it, for water will flow out and the cauterizer should be of this shape.
Then cauterize the legs twice on each leg, with the knife-edge of the cauterizer. One cauterization should be below the knee and the other above it towards the middle of the thigh. On each buttock, cauterize twice.
Leave the cauterization open without treatment for a long time until water flows out from it, then treat it with what has been mentioned.
The Thirty-third Chapter
In the Treatment of Diarrhea
If diarrhea is due to cold and humidity, causing weakness of the digestive powers in the stomach and intestines, despite various treatments, and you see that the patient is suitable for cauterization with great strength, then cauterize them once on the abdomen. As mentioned earlier in cauterization of the stomach with a ring cauterizer, and four cauterizations around the navel with a gently heated, round cauterizer. Also, one cauterization on the pubic hair or two if necessary.
If you find that humidity is abundant and the patient is suitable for it, cauterize once on the pubic hair, once on each rib cage, and perhaps add two small cauterizations on the stomach near the large intestine. This treatment will be successful without fail, if Allah wills.
The Thirty-fourth Chapter
In the Treatment of Hemorrhoids
If there are chronic, numerous or single hemorrhoids in the anus, caused by coarse, cold impurities or corrupt humors, and they have been treated with what was mentioned earlier without success, then cauterize the patient three times on the lower back near the spine, about a finger's breadth below the waist.
Place two fingers beneath the breast, assuming his stomach has cooled and his food is undigested. Observe his face which appears pale, therefore apply a cupping glass to his stomach as mentioned earlier, and another on his chest. And place an iron branding tool on his hip and leave the cupping glass open for a time, then treat him until he recovers, if Allah wills.
Chapter Thirty-Five.
On Treating Warts.
After cutting it off, if the mole is cut, heat the cauterizing iron resembling a nail and insert its tip into the same wound of the removed mole. Press your hand firmly until the iron reaches the mouth of the vein from which blood flows. Perform this once or twice.
If there are many warts, cauterize each one as described earlier, then treat them with appropriate ointments until they heal. If the cautery is performed on cotton, it will be more effective.
Chapter Thirty-Six
On Treating Hemorrhoids That Appear in the Anus and Its Surroundings.
If the patient does not respond to diet and the treatment described earlier, then perhaps cautery may help. If one suffers from prolapsed hemorrhoids with pus and foul discharge issuing forth, first measure it using a fine probe.
Then determine its size using the probe, heat the cauterizing iron resembling a nail, and insert its tip into the same hemorrhoid vertically according to its depth and the measure of the probe. Perform cautery until all corrupt tissues are burned once, twice, or thrice depending on your need.
And be cautious not to burn the nerve if there is one, nor the great vein if there is one. If the hemorrhoids reach the bladder or the rectum.
Avoid these areas altogether. Perform this procedure only if the hemorrhoids are in a fleshy spot and you estimate that they are not prolapsed. Treat the area until it heals. If the wound closes, the materials stop flowing, and this state persists for some time, then know that it is completely healed.
If the discharge does not cease, know that it is either issuing from a fractured bone or a large diseased cavity, or something similar which will be mentioned in its proper place.
Chapter Seven and Thirty.
In the matter of the kidneys.
If pain occurs in the kidneys due to cold or strong wind, and sexual activity is thereby diminished, then cauterize on both sides of the same kidney using the triangular cautery iron mentioned earlier; perhaps a third one may be added on the same plate, making three triangles arranged symmetrically, which would increase its effectiveness.
Chapter Eighty-Three
In the matter of the bladder.
If weakness and relaxation occur in the bladder due to cold and dampness such that the patient cannot retain urine, cauterize on the lower part of the scrotum over the bladder where pubic hair begins, and also cauterize once on the right side of the scrotum and once on the left side.
And after cauterizing each side, cauterize to the extent of the thumb joint, and cauterize once on the lower back or twice if necessary; use the triangular cautery iron mentioned earlier.
Chapter Ninety-Three
In the matter of cauterizing the uterus.
If cold and dampness cause material to flow from the uterus, preventing conception and impairing fertility or causing pain upon intercourse, then cauterize three times around the scrotum as mentioned earlier in the case of bladder cautery. And cauterize once on cotton placed on the lower back or twice; use the triangular cautery iron.
Chapter Forty
In cauterizing dislocation of the hip joint.
If wrongful dampness enters the hip joint causing dislocation, and the leg appears longer than the other when compared side by side with a gap felt at the point of dislocation, then cauterize on the hip joint itself using a semicircular cautery iron.
After drawing a semicircle around the joint with ink, cauterize using the cautery iron depicted earlier for cauterizing the stomach; if this iron is not available, use three large circular cautery irons.
It is recommended to incise deeply according to the thickness of all the skin, then treat it until it heals, God willing.
Chapter Forty-One.
In treating hemorrhoids.
If pain occurs in the buttock region due to coldness and dampness, as mentioned earlier in this section, but the treatment has not been effective after some time, it is advisable for the physician to thin out the thick humors using rhubarb or tragacanth gum.
Then, cauterize and direct the cut towards the buttock in two ways: either cauterize with burning drugs or cauterize with fire. Cauterizing with fire can be done in many ways; one of them is to perform three similar cauteries on the actual buttock.
And make it deep enough, with about the thickness of a finger between each cautery. Use a copper cauterizing instrument. You may also perform one cautery in the center at the very top of the buttock, making four in total. If desired, you can use the circular cautery mentioned earlier for dislocated buttocks to perform one cautery.
This is the description of cauterizing for hemorrhoids if the pain is persistent in the buttock itself without extending to the thigh or leg.
But if the pain extends to the thigh and leg, cauterize twice on the thigh at the location indicated by the patient's complaint of pain, and once above the anus about four fingers to the right side using a sharp cautery. The depth of the cut should be according to the thickness of the skin only.
If the pain extends towards the toes of the foot, cauterize there three or four times with a pointed cautery as needed. If the pain is indicated beneath the knee towards the leg, cauterize there once with a sharp cautery.
And be careful in all your cauteries to avoid reaching the sciatic nerve or a major artery, as this would cause great harm or disability to the patient.
I have seen two people who cauterized above the anus too deeply, causing the leg to swell up to the foot and become gangrenous. The entire limb was ruined, and afterwards diarrhea and death occurred. If the pain is on both sides, cauterize them according to this same method.
It has been mentioned by some wise scholars that this type of hip dislocation resembles a cup made of iron, with its diameter being half a cubit and at its mouth it is slightly thicker than the stone of a date or a little less. Within this cup there are two smaller cups.
And between each pair of cups it is the width of a thumb joint, with both cups being open on either side and their height being approximately one or two finger joints. They have iron handles that are securely attached to the cups.
Then they are heated in fire until red-hot and the sparks are removed. They are then placed on the hip joint, with the patient lying on their healthy side, and three circular movements are made at once. This process is left for three days, after which the wound is smeared with butter and kept open.
Thereafter, treat it with ointment until it heals. The author of this book says that this type of dislocation is rarely used due to its severity and the unpleasant sight it presents, and because few people can endure it except those who have strong endurance and are willing to bear it.
As for dislocation caused by burning drugs, two cups resembling doors' bolts made of copper or iron should be prepared.
Their height should be about one and a half finger joints, with the width between them being as thick as a finger. Both ends should be open, and they should be fixed together in this manner.
Then place them on the hip joint while the patient lies on their healthy side, with your hand wrapped in cotton. Pour hot water between the two cups using a funnel and hold it for about an hour, until the patient endures the pain and heat.
Until the pain subsides, then remove your hand with the tool and wipe off all the hot water from the hip joint using cold water. Leave it for three days, applying butter to it until the blackness of the burn fades away. Leave it open for as long as pus keeps coming out.
Then treat it with ointment until it heals. If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a similar device for them as you did for the hip joint using hot water. This is the description of the hot water mixture which has been proven effective in treating ailments.
Take from saltpeter and from unslaked lime one part each, grind them together, and place them in a new vessel pierced at the bottom with a small hole sufficient to admit the wick. Place underneath the vessel another vessel perforated in like manner.
Pour on the saltpeter and lime some fresh water to cover them by a finger's breadth, then press them with your hand using a good press. Leave the vessel until the harsh water has drained into the lower perforated vessel, then collect all this water and pour it on two more portions of saltpeter and lime likewise prepared.
Then it becomes very caustic and can be used in many medical operations and cauterizations of various organs, as it acts like fire itself. Among the remedies with which one may cauterize a joint are Thapsia, bdellium resin, and lime mixed with soap, all ground finely.
Galenos relates a story about an elderly man who used this remedy to treat pain in the hip joint and sciatica, finding it extremely effective and claiming that no further treatment was needed as it cured him at once.
So much so that he might have entered the bathhouse carried and come out cured, using green frankincense; if this is not available, fresh dry frankincense may be used instead. Grind it with a little fat and apply it to the hip joint or thigh where the pain is felt.
Let it remain for three hours or until the patient feels that the burning sensation has subsided, then take him to the bathhouse. When his body is dry, immerse him in a warm bath. If the pain goes away and he is cured, with God's permission, if not, repeat the application after ten days.
Insha'Allah, he will be cured. Know that one should not apply cautery with these drugs unless the body has been purged beforehand. Diskarides mentions that burnt goat hair can also be used to cauterize sciatica.
The cauterization process is as follows: Take some wool, soak it in old oil and apply it to the deep hollow between the thumb and the wrist bone, closer to the wrist. Then take dry goat hair.
Kindle it with fire until it becomes a ember, then place it on wool and let it cool until it extinguishes. Then take another one; continue doing this until the pain subsides from the elbow to the hip by the permission of Allah. This type of cupping is called 'Al-Ba'ri'.

In treating back pain.
Back pain may have many causes, such as falls, blows, or excessive coughing and the like. In this type of cupping, it is only performed when there is a buildup of cold wet matter.
After the patient has coughed up phlegm, they should be cupped on their back where the pain is. There should be three rows of cups across the width of the table, with five or more cups in each row depending on the patient's tolerance and strength.
The cupping should be done using a cupping horn, using three or four cups for best results. A medium-sized brass cup can also be used, shaped like this:

In cupping the initial rise of the buttocks
This condition often affects young children. The first sign in a child is difficulty breathing during movement and activity, and you will find that the last few vertebrae of their spine have protruded like a bead, standing out from the others.
If you see this and wish to stop it, cup with a circular cup shaped like this: Take the cupping on both sides of the vertebra evenly.
