Section Twenty-Three
In excising impacted teeth.
Teeth, if they grow in a manner other than their natural course, mar the beauty of the face, especially when this happens to women or young boys. Therefore, it should be examined; if the tooth has grown from behind another tooth.
And if it cannot be extracted nor pushed back, cut it off with this instrument which resembles this image:
It resembles a small beak and should be made of Indian steel, very sharp at the tip. Cutting should take place over many days due to the hardness of the tooth and to avoid shaking other teeth. But if it is protruding and can be extracted, extract it with a pair of forceps which resembles this image.
It should all be made of iron with the tip being very thinly crafted like a needle. Warm the tooth gently over many days using this pair of forceps to prevent shaking and falling out of the tooth, then grasp it firmly and remove its covering with some tweezers.
If a tooth has broken off some of its part causing discomfort to the tongue while speaking, then it should also be warmed gently until that roughness disappears and becomes smooth without causing discomfort to the tongue nor hindering speech.
Section Thirty-Three
On binding loose teeth with silver or gold threads.
If the front teeth are loose due to an impact or fall and the patient cannot chew food without them falling out, despite treatment with astringent medications that have not been effective.
Then, bind them with a thread of gold or silver; gold is better because silver tends to tarnish and corrode over time. The thread should be moderate in thickness, neither too thin nor too thick according to the space between the teeth.
The method of binding is to take the thread and insert its loop between the two healthy teeth, then stitch it through the gap between the loose teeth until the stitching reaches the other side of the healthy teeth.
Then you return the suture to the side where it began, gently and wisely pulling your hand so that it does not move at all; your tension on the thread should be at the roots of the teeth so that it does not slip. Then you cut off the excess ends of the thread with scissors, gather them together and twist them with tweezers, concealing them between the sound tooth and the displaced one.
Lest the tongue be harmed, then you leave it like this tied until it remains thus forever. If it breaks or its tension slackens, reinforce it with another thread and it will remain thus for all eternity. This is an image of the teeth and their arrangement in two sound teeth and two displaced ones as you see:
And a single tooth or both may return to their places after falling out, becoming fixed as described above and remaining so. Indeed, this is the work of a skilled craftsman, who can even carve bone from oxen in the shape of teeth and place it where the tooth has gone missing. And he ties it as we have said, and it remains thus forever.
Chapter Forty-Three
In the cutting of the frenulum that hinders speech.
This frenulum under the tongue may be either natural, present at birth, or accidental, resulting from a wound that has healed.
The procedure is to open the patient's mouth and elevate their head in your lap, then raise their tongue and cut across the frenulum until the tongue is released from its restraint. If it is somewhat hard and complex, being a result of scar tissue from a healed wound, then incise it with scissors and cut across until the frenulum is severed and the ties are loosened.
And beware that the incision is not too deep, lest you cut a blood vessel there and cause bleeding. Then rinse with rosewater or vinegar and cold water after the cutting. And place under the tongue a wick of cotton for the patient to hold in their mouth each night.
Lest it adhere again. If bleeding occurs, apply powdered gum tragacanth to the place. If bleeding persists, cauterize the area with a suitable glass spatula. Then treat him with all kinds of treatment until he recovers.
Chapter Thirty-Five
In expelling the toad born under the tongue.
A tumor resembling a small toad may occur under the tongue, preventing it from its natural function and perhaps filling the mouth entirely. The procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth towards the sun and observe the tumor.
If it appears red or black, hard, and insensitive to touch, do not intervene for it is cancerous. However, if it tends towards whiteness with dampness present, pierce it with a fine needle and cut it out with scissors from all sides.
If bleeding troubles you during the procedure, sprinkle powdered bdellium on it until the bleeding stops. Then resume your work until you remove it entirely. Then rinse with vinegar and salt.
Then treat him with appropriate remedies until he recovers.
Chapter Thirty-Six
On treating a swelling of the tonsils.
And if a growth appears within the throat, resembling the glands that appear externally and are called tonsils, and does not heal with the remedies mentioned in the previous section...
If the tumor is hard, dark in color, and insensitive to touch, do not treat it with an iron instrument. If it is red in color and its origin is thick, also do not treat it with an iron instrument for fear of bleeding. Leave it alone until it ripens, either to fall off or to burst on its own.
But if it is white, rounded, and its origin is thin, this is what should be cut. First, ensure that the heat of the tumor has subsided completely or somewhat before proceeding with the procedure.
Then seat the patient facing the sun, with his head in your lap. Open his mouth and take a spatula in your hand, using it to press down on his tongue as follows:
Make a thin silver or copper spatula, like a blade. Press it on the tongue to reveal the tumor and then pierce it with a fine needle and pull it out as much as possible without damaging any surrounding tissues.
Then it is cut with this tool, its shape resembling scissors, but with curved ends, each one sharp against the other. It is made of Indian iron or Damascus steel.
If this tool is not available, then cut it with a probe, which resembles this shape
Sharp on one side and not sharp on the other. After cutting one gland, cut the other in the same manner. Then, rinse the patient with cold water or vinegar and water.
If there is bleeding, rinse with water in which pomegranate peel or oak leaves have been steeped until the bleeding stops. Then treat it until it heals. There may also grow other tumors in the throat besides the tonsils; these are to be cut as mentioned for cutting the tonsils.
I treated a woman for a tumor that had grown inside her throat, striking the epiglottis with little sensation. It almost completely blocked her throat, causing her to breathe through a narrow passage and preventing her from eating or drinking.
She was near death, having only one or two days left to live. The tumor had grown so large that two branches of it protruded from her nostrils. I acted quickly and inserted a probe into one of the branches, then pulled it out, removing a suitable piece of the growth.
Then I cut it where I reached it from the nostril. Then I did the same with what protruded from the other nostril. Then I opened her mouth, pushed down her tongue, inserted the probe into the tumor itself and cut off a piece of it without causing much bleeding.
The woman's throat cleared immediately, and she began drinking water right away. Then she was able to eat again. We continued cutting the tumor repeatedly over a long period of time, but it kept growing back.
So she recovered and the tumor in her throat ceased to grow larger, then she left the area and I do not know what happened to her after that.
Chapter Seventy-Three
In cutting tumors of the uvula
If a swelling appears on the uvula, which resembles an ant (thus named "ubna"), and does not respond to treatment with what has been mentioned regarding division
I saw the hot tumor had subsided and was thin, it should not be cut; for it was not solid and round nor long, and its color was not bloody or black nor did it have any sensation. Therefore, it should be avoided from being cut.
If there is growth in the patient, then if you see it with the characteristics mentioned of whiteness and length, let the patient sit beside the sun and press his tongue with the tool that has been described before, then insert the trocar into the vein.
And pull it downwards and cut it with one of the tools mentioned for cutting tonsils. Do not cut more than what is beyond its natural size, otherwise you would harm the voice and speech.
Then after cutting, use what we described for cutting tonsils and treat it until it heals. If the patient is reluctant to cut it, do not resort to trickery without caution; the face of the deceit in this case is the sharp drug, which is putting the head of the patient into a millstone.
Then press his tongue with the tool mentioned, then take from the sharp water mentioned in the chapter on cupping and knead it with a glowing iron not extinguished, making it neither thick nor thin, and fill this tool with it. This is its shape:
It has a tip for placing the drug like the concavity of a spoon, and you place the tool with the drug on the tonsil itself while the patient lies on his side so that no saliva from within his throat falls into it to harm him.
Then hold your hand with the drug and press it on the tonsil for half an hour until you see that it has turned black and the burning sensation has subsided. If you wish, wrap a piece of linen around the tip of a spoon and dip it in the drug.
Then insert the spoon with the linen into a tube from above until the linen sticks to the tonsil. Do this repeatedly until you reach the desired amount of cupping, then leave it alone; it will dry and fall off after three or four days. If you need to repeat the drug, prepare it again.
After cauterization, wipe around the tonsil with a linen soaked in sesame oil and use it to wipe away any surrounding medicine. Then rinse with cold water and treat externally with poultices and internally with gargling until healed; this method is safer than cutting and far from causing fear.
The tonsils can also be treated gently without cautery or cutting by applying incense made according to this method: take equal amounts of fleawort, saffron, savory, sage, hyssop, opopanax and similar herbs, grind them together in a mortar with vinegar.
Melt the mixture in an earthenware pot over a slow fire, stirring with the pestle of wisdom. In the center of the lid make a hole through which to insert the siphon apparatus made of silver or copper according to this method:.
Insert the tip containing the wick into the patient's mouth until the vapor reaches the tonsils via the tube, thoroughly steaming them. Repeat this several times until they soften. Avoid using this treatment at the onset of the swelling.
For if you do this at the onset of swelling, it will often increase its size. Rather, wait until the hot swelling has subsided. If you do not have this apparatus, take a reed and insert a thin egg shell into one end to prevent the patient's mouth from burning.
For the eggshell prevents the hot vapor from burning the mouth, making this a safe and effective treatment:.
Chapter Eighty-Three
In extracting splinters and other foreign bodies from the throat.
Often, bone or fish spines, among other things, become lodged in the throat. It is necessary to remove what can be seen clearly after pressing down the tongue using an instrument held in the sun:.
So that you can see clearly what is in the throat, and if something cannot be seen, make the patient vomit before digestion begins in the stomach. Perhaps the lodged object will come out with the vomiting or can be dislodged with a piece of soft cloth or gauze soaked in olive oil:.
Or, use a piece of dry bread soaked in oil or take a piece of soft sea sponge tied to a thread and insert it until it reaches the location of the spine. Then quickly pull out the thread several times:.
Frequently, the bone or splinter remains attached and does not come out; if it does not come out as mentioned previously, then use an instrument made of lead in this form:
The instrument should be slightly thicker than a needle and have a hook at its end which the patient inserts into their throat gently while raising their head upwards, taking care not to touch the throat so as not to cause coughing. The doctor may also insert it with his hand,
And the patient should preferably use it themselves, as they know better the location of the foreign body and can push it downwards or pull it upwards with the instrument according to what is comfortable for them until it comes out,
Chapter Thirty-Nine.
On Removing Foreign Bodies from the Throat.
If treating the foreign body with medication as mentioned earlier does not work, then look into the patient's throat when they face the sun after pressing down their tongue with the instrument described above.
If you see the foreign body, then remove it using a small tweezers or a gentle hook. If you cannot manage this, then take a hollow tube and insert it into the patient's throat close to the foreign body. Then introduce an iron rod heated in fire into the tube.
Do this several times while the patient refrains from drinking water all day. Then, they should take a cup filled with cold water, open their mouth in it, swish the water around, and spit it out without swallowing any. They should shake the water occasionally.
If the foreign body does not come out as described, then fumigate the throat with hot water and use the instrument mentioned earlier to fumigate it with incense. Do this several times until it falls out.
The purpose of using incense is to take a quantity of it and light it with fire. The incense should be placed in a container covered with a lid having a hole in its center. Insert the tip of the instrument into this hole, then place the incense on it. The patient should put their mouth over the other end of the tube and close it tightly so that no smoke escapes until they feel the warmth of the incense reaching their throat.

Chapter Forty.
In it is discussed the use of speech for crushing and breaking down tumors.
The types of tumors are many and varied, as mentioned one by one in this book. They differ in their hardness and softness from two aspects: firstly, the nature of the tumor itself, and secondly, the fluids it contains.
And the second aspect is due to the locations where they occur in the body, for a tumor that occurs in the head is not like one that occurs in the buttocks, nor is a tumor that occurs in an inflamed area like one that occurs in a joint; each has its own ruling regarding treatment.
Among tumors, some should not be crushed until the pus within them has fully ripened and completed its maturation. Others should be crushed even if the pus is still unripe, such as those that are close to joints.
For if a tumor occurs near a joint and persists until it becomes gangrenous around it, it may corrupt the ligaments or nerves of that joint, causing paralysis of the limb, or the tumor may be located near an important organ.
For if you delay crushing it until it fully ripens, you will have harmed the main organ nearby, or it may be located near the buttocks; in this case, crush it while it is still unripe. But it is necessary to crush only those tumors that are not fully ripe and located near the buttocks, lest gangrene should set in and penetrate into the rectum, causing corruption.
It is sometimes the case that it does not heal, and one should know the time of eruption of tumors that have fully grown; this occurs during quietness when the pain of the tumor subsides, fever abates, redness diminishes, pulsation stops, and the head of the tumor becomes soft.
It is preferable to incise the tumor at its lowest point if possible, so that the discharge flows downwards more easily or in a softer part of the tumor; and if the tumors are near the hands or feet, let the incision be made along the length of the body.
And in places where muscles, tendons, nerves, and vessels are situated, and generally in all flat places without bending, one should follow the line of that place; but if it is a fatty tumor, it is better to leave it alone.
Until it becomes fully matured as mentioned before; for if its incision is made earlier, much discharge will flow out from it and it may be dirty and foul-smelling with hard edges and base. Some tumors may be incised across the body width when necessary or according to what the organ needs.
It is preferable to use a single incision for small tumors and a wide one or many incisions according to the size of large tumors. Some tumors may require circumcision and cutting of the skin if it has become like a rag.
And sometimes, death occurs as mentioned in many books and cases, including those where an incision with three corners is made or a tumor is cut in the shape of an oak leaf.
And in some cases, a round or crescent-shaped incision may be used, and for smooth, flat tumors without a head, only a simple incision should be made. If the tumor is very large with much accumulation of matter and has been incised, it is preferable not to rush so that all the pus does not come out at once.
Rather, some of it should be taken out first, then the tumor should be tied for another day before removing more pus; this process can be repeated gradually until all of it is removed.
And particularly if the patient is weak in strength, a pregnant woman, an infant or an elderly man, the vital spirit often dissipates with the sudden discharge of pus, perhaps causing death to the patient while you are unaware. Be warned of this chapter most severely.
After removing these tumors, it is necessary to cleanse the wound and observe; if the tumor's cut is small or its breach is simple, then use gauze or cotton wadding; but if the tumor is large and the abdominal wounds are many.
It is necessary to insert a wick into each breach until they reach one another; if some of the tumor's skin or cortex has been severed, it should be stuffed with dry cotton wool or bandages made from gauze and tied in place for three days.
Then remove it and treat it with the appropriate ointments until it heals. If bleeding occurs during your work, use cold water and vinegar, soaked in a cotton cloth and applied to the bleeding site repeatedly.
If bleeding persists, then employ the methods and treatments and dressings described in many places throughout this book and its sections; particularly if it is wintertime and the tumor site has abundant blood vessels, then apply heated linseed oil plaster.
And apply it to the site. If it is summertime and the sites are fleshy, then carry linseed oil plasters soaked in cold water and oil or water and oil until the third day, as mentioned earlier, when you should remove the tumor and cleanse it.
And use similar treatments until it heals. This is the general knowledge of treating tumors that you need, and I have mentioned specifically how to treat each type in a concise manner.

Chapter Forty-Three.
In a cut to the throat due to an internal throat tumor.
The ancients mentioned this cut in the throat, but I have not seen anyone in our land perform it. However, those suffering from angina should avoid cutting the throat as they derive no benefit from it.
To make all the vessels and lungs clear, but for those with a hot tumor in the mouth, throat, or tonsils that is not due to tracheal cause, it is necessary to use the cut in the throat to escape suffocation.
It is necessary, if one wishes to do so, to cut the throat beneath three or four small circles of the tracheal rings, not on the cartilage, in a manner similar to the opening of the peritoneum, at this location.
Because it is fleshless and the blood vessels are far away, if the operator is timid, he should extend the skin of the throat with a probe before cutting the skin until he reaches the trachea, avoiding the blood vessels if he sees any.

I found that the blood coming from the wound was slow, so I knew it had not cut an artery or vein. The wind was escaping from the wound, so I dressed and sutured it, treating it until it healed. Nothing else happened to the servant except a slight hoarseness.
And she returned after some days to her original state. Hence we say that cutting the throat is not harmful.

Chapter Forty-Four: On incising the swelling that appears externally on the neck, known as goiter of the neck.
This tumor called 'goiter of the neck' is a large tumor the color of the skin, and it is common in women. It has two types.
Either it is natural and there is no remedy for it, or it is adventitious and has two types: one similar to fatty tumors, and the other similar to tumors caused by the twisting of the carotid artery, which is dangerous to incise. Chapter Fifty-Four
In Fissure on Kinds of Goods.
The goods are many, and all kinds have been mentioned in the division. Now we should explain the difference between goods and excrescences, as it is confusing. I say that an excrescence is accompanied by heat, fever, and severe pain until the inflammation subsides. And the swelling subsides, at which point the fever and severity abate. A good does not accompany heat, fever, or pain, and it is contained within a capsule called the peritoneum, which is its special covering. Its appearance is like that of an ulceration, becoming larger or smaller than a chickpea.
And it is of two kinds: either fatty or containing moisture, with various colors as mentioned in the division. Therefore, when treating a good, you should first probe and examine it using the instrument called the probe, whose image appears in the following chapter.
Determine the size of the tumor, then remove the probe and observe what comes out as a result. If moist matter of any color emerges, cut it with a simple incision as mentioned in other tumors. But if no moist matter emerges upon removing the probe, know that it is fatty.
Cut it with a cross-shaped incision like this, as I have shown you. Suspend it from the forceps and gently strip the skin from all sides, taking care to preserve the capsule along with the good if possible.
But if the capsule breaks during the procedure and you are unable to remove it intact, this happens frequently. Remove it piece by piece until nothing remains. For if any part of it remains, it will likely recur.
If you are unable to remove it completely, cauterize the wound with some caustic powder. Then close the wound and apply something that cools the inflammation. Treat it with other remedies until it heals. If the good is large, sew its lips together and treat it with ointments.
If profuse or non-profuse bleeding occurs during the procedure, quickly cauterize the area with powdered pitch. Leave it for two or three days until the wound becomes infected and the bleeding subsides. Then return to removing any remaining good.

Chapter Forty-Nine
In cutting a swelling that appears due to an artery or vein, called anurusma.
If the artery is injured and its skin above becomes detached, swelling often results from that, likewise if a vein presents with inflammation and swelling.
The signs by which it is known whether the swelling and inflammation are due to an artery or a vein: if it is from an artery, it will be rectangular and concentrated deep in the body; if you press on the swelling with your finger, it feels like there's a crunching sound.
What is from the vein will be a round swelling on the surface of the body; cutting into these swellings is dangerous, especially those in the armpit, groin, neck, and other many places on the body. They are often very large and should not be avoided treatment with iron cautery.
And those that are in the extremities or head should also not be avoided. If it is from an arterial aneurysm, cut along its length on the skin, then open the cut with forceps and tie off the artery and cleanse it of adventitia.

The swelling will subside and then use treatment that brings about suppuration until the ligatures fall off, then treat it with suitable plasters until it heals.
If the swelling is due to a vein cut, grasp as much of it with your hand as possible along with its skin; then insert a needle underneath from where you grasped it, passing through it with a doubled thread until it exits on the other side. Then tie it to the tumor with a good knot, as you have been instructed for tying an artery from both ends of the thread; but if you fear that the threads may slip out, insert another needle with another thread beneath the entire tumor where the first needle crosses.
Tighten your threads in four places, then incise the tumor in its middle until what is inside comes out. Cut off a piece of skin, and leave what remains tied, then apply a dressing soaked in a mixture of wine and oil. Then employ the treatment with wound dressings and ointments until it heals,
Chapter Fifty.
On tumors arising from nerve twisting.
Just as a tumor can appear in an artery or vein, so too can a tumor appear in a nerve if it is struck or fatigued excessively, particularly in the regions of the wrists and ankles.
And in every place where joints move, there can appear a soft tumor similar in color to the rest of the body; it is usually painless, but upon pressing it firmly, the patient may feel numbness like that caused by pressure. Such tumors are not localized deep within the body.
But such tumors are under the skin, moving in all directions except towards the front or back. Those located in joints should not be treated with iron, as it may cause bruising. Tumors in the head or forehead should also be avoided.
Then cut the skin with a scalpel. If the tumor is small, grasp it with forceps and excise it at its base. If it is large, suspend it with a hook, incise it, remove it, and close the wound with sutures. Treat until healed.
Chapter Fifty-One.
On the removal of moles appearing on the abdomen.
Many people have moles appearing on their bellies and other parts of the body, called "natural" ones because they resemble mushrooms. Their roots are thin, but their heads are thick; sometimes their lips turn inwards, and they can be small or large.
I have seen a man with moles on his belly resembling mushrooms, both white and thin at their base but with turned-in lips and cracked surfaces from which moisture constantly flowed. I removed them; one weighed about eighteen ounces, the other about six.
The procedure for removing it involves examining [the patient], and if the patient is moist and the color of the nevus is white, wet, and soft in origin, then cut it off with a broad scalpel. Have cauterizing irons ready nearby, for much blood often flows during its removal.
However, if blood overpowers you during its removal, cauterize it. If the patient is cowardly and fears being cut with iron, then take a strong iron thread and tie it around the nevus which has this description; leave it for two days, then tighten the iron thread further until it continues to tighten.
Whenever the thread tightens upon the nevus until it breaks off and falls by itself without pain. However, in cutting thick nevi, especially those on the abdomen, there may be some fear and difficulty; yet, it is possible to cut half or part of it.
Then cauterize it to prevent its return, then treat it until the wound heals. Beware of cutting a nevus that is dark-colored, insensitive to touch, and unsightly; for it is a cancerous tumor, which we will mention later.
Chapter Fifty-Two.
On the treatment of pimples.
Pimples occur due to many causes, either from a rupture of the peritoneum on the abdomen causing hernias or from intestines as mentioned in other sections, or from blood flowing from a vein or artery as stated earlier, or from wind trapped therein.
If it is due to a rupture of the peritoneum and herniation, then the color of the tumor will resemble that of the body, it will be soft without pain, and its appearance will differ with changing positions. If it is due to herniation of the intestines, its appearance will differ greatly as described earlier. When pressed with fingers, it disappears then returns; there may be gurgling sounds and it becomes much larger during exertion or hot baths. If it is due to dampness, it will feel soft.
If it is not due to blood, when pressed with the hand it will not disappear or increase or decrease in size. If it is due to a fatty tumor, then it will be hard and solid, maintaining its original size.
If the pain has come from wind, then its touch is pleasant to us, and the treatment for this is: if you find that the source of the pain comes from blood in a vein or artery or wind, then it is advisable not to treat it, as there is fear and danger involved, as I informed you earlier in the chapter on tumors caused by veins and arteries.
If the pain comes from the bowels or bladder, you should order the patient to hold themselves upright while standing and then draw around the painful area with ink. Then order him to lie on his back between your hands, then make a wide incision around the painful area with a scalpel where you drew with ink, then insert a large probe into the center of the swelling upwards, and tightly bind the site of the incision with strong thread or silk suture.
Then tie the ligament like a noose, open it in the middle of the tense swelling above the ligament, insert your index finger into it, and seek the bowel. If the ligament has taken it, loosen the noose and push the bowel back into the abdomen. If you find a bladder, dilate it with a probe.
And cut its stalk, if an artery or vein obstructs you, ligate it properly and return to your task. Take two needles with strong threads attached, insert them into the incision around the swelling in a cross shape, then pull the swelling in four places using the needles.
If you wish, remove the needles and leave the site until the tense flesh rots and falls off on its own, or cut it if it softens and rots. Then treat it with appropriate ointments until it heals, if the pain is from flesh that has grown there.
Or if it's from moisture, you should cauterize the swelling as mentioned earlier, then remove the blood or moisture found there and treat it with something that adheres to the site.

In treating cancer.

If I can heal anyone of it, let no one precede me to that, and the procedure is, if it is movable as mentioned, to proceed gradually removing the black spots one by one, then separate it if it is filled with blood vessels.

But squeeze the areas and remove all thick blood with your hand or whatever instruments are available. If great bleeding occurs during the operation due to cutting an artery or vein, tie the vessel until the bleeding stops, then treat it with other remedies until it heals.

Chapter Sixty-Five
In the case of a boil that appears on the eyelid, eyelash, and blackness and corruption with adhesion of the eyelid to the eye.

Chapter Seventy-Five
In the purification of infants and treating them for any afflictions they may face.
Circumcision is nothing but separating contact like other surgeries except that since it is done by us willingly and for the sake of children especially, we must perform it in the best manner.
The easiest way leading to safety is, as I say, the ancient authorities did not mention circumcision in any of their books because it was not practiced among them; rather, it is something that we have acquired.
By experience, for I have found the majority of craftsmen and barbers practicing circumcision with Moses' tool and scissors, using the bandage and tying with thread and cutting with fingernail, having tried all these methods.
I did not find better than using scissors for the cutting and tying with thread because the use of Moses' tool often results in damaging the skin since the foreskin has two layers, so sometimes only the upper layer is cut while the lower one remains.
Therefore, one is forced to cut again and endure more pain, and the use of the file does not ensure that the tip of the urethra will not be cut because it may enter into its hole, while cutting with fingernail might cause skin to slip and spoil your work or perhaps the child's foreskin was naturally short.
Therefore, many are born that way and do not require circumcision, as I have seen, but the experience has shown me the superiority of using scissors and tying with thread because the blade above is equal to the blade below.
So when you press your hand with both blades together, cutting evenly and at once, the thread becomes like a wall surrounding the urethra from all sides without any error happening, and the first step of the procedure is to calm the child.
Especially if the child is one of those who understand little, so that you may reassure him by explaining to him that you will only tie a thread around his urethra today and leave it until another day, then release it and stroke him gently in any way he accepts, then make him stand before you upright.
Let him not be seated and hide the scissors in his sleeve or underfoot, so that the boy's eyes do not fall upon them at all, nor on any of the instruments. Then insert your hand into his anus and inflate the skin and draw it upwards until the head of the anus appears.
Then clean it from whatever filth may be found in it. Then bind the known place with a doubled thread. Then bind a little below it with another bandage. Then grasp the lower binding firmly with your thumb and index finger, and cut between the bindings. Then lift the skin upwards quickly and bring out the head of the anus. Then let the blood flow a little, for it is better and causes less swelling. Then wipe it with a moist cloth, then sprinkle on it some powdered dried colocynth, which is the best I have tried, or fine barley flour, which is also good.

The Fifty-Eighth Chapter
In treating retained urine in the bladder.
If retained urine in the bladder occurs due to obstruction by a stone, coagulated blood, pus, or flesh growth and similar conditions, treat it with the methods of treatment mentioned in the previous sections.
And if the urine does not flow, and you find that its retention is due to a stone stuck in the neck of the bladder, then have the patient kneel with their buttocks raised. Then have another person sit on their back, pressing the abdomen towards the back, while the patient holds themselves steady as much as possible.
At this point, the neck of the bladder will push the stone backwards and urine will flow. If it does not flow with what was mentioned, and the condition becomes severe for the patient, then use the instrument called a 'qathathir' to remove it, which looks like this:
It is made of silver and thin, smooth and flexible like the tube of a bird's feather in its gentle slope. It is about one and a half spans long and has a slight funnel at its tip. To use it for drawing urine, take a doubled thread and tie a piece of sponge or cotton to its end securely.
Insert the tip of the thread into the bottom of the qathathir, then cut off any excess sponge with scissors so that it fits snugly inside like a cork. Then grease the qathathir with oil, foam, or egg white and have the patient sit on a chair.
Then expose the patient's urethra and anoint it with moistened cotton, oil, or warm water. Then gently insert the qathathir into the urethra until it reaches the neck of the bladder. Then bend the urethra upwards towards the scrotum and push the qathathir further inside.
Until the urethra is bent, then push the qathathir further inside until it reaches near the bladder. Then tilt the penis downwards and push the qathathir until the patient feels that it has reached an empty space.
It is done in this manner because the passage through which urine flows is bent, then the thread is inserted into the catheter with some force; for urine follows the catheter upon its removal, and water flows out.
Continue until the bladder empties and the patient feels relief.
Chapter Fifty-Nine.
How to inject the bladder with sitz bath.

And the hollow space into which the catheter is inserted should fit snugly without any excess so that when it is pulled, moisture will be drawn in, and when it is pushed, liquid will be expelled just like how a siphon works to throw oil onto naval battles.

For that liquid reaches the bladder immediately so that the patient feels it, and this is an image of a fine syringe used for bladder irrigation:
It is made of silver or brass, with its upper end resembling a small funnel and having a groove underneath for the ribbon. Then take a camel's bladder and fill it with the liquid you wish to irrigate the bladder with, then tie it tightly between the grooves using a double thread.

Chapter Sixty.
In the removal of stones.
We have already mentioned in the division the types of stones and their treatment with drugs, and the difference between stones formed in the kidneys and those formed in the bladder, and all its signs. And we have mentioned stones that require manual extraction and cutting.
And this is a specific stone formed in the bladder, which lodges in the urethra; I will describe it clearly and concisely.
I say that stones formed in the bladder are more common among children, and one of its signs is that urine comes out of the bladder like water in its smoothness.
And in it sand appears and the penis is irritated and troubled by it, and it often prolapses then retracts. The anus also protrudes in many cases. It is easy for boys to pass stones until they reach fourteen years of age, but difficult for the elderly. For youths, it is moderate between these extremes.
And the larger the stones are, the easier their treatment. Conversely, small stones are more difficult to treat. So when we begin treatment, it is necessary first to administer an enema to remove all the feces in the rectum, as it may obstruct the passage of the stone during examination.
Then take the patient by both legs, shake and drop him downwards so that the stone descends to the neck of the bladder, or have him jump from a high place repeatedly. Then sit him down in front of you with his legs spread and hands under his thighs so that the bladder is entirely tilted downwards. Then examine him.
Feel him from the outside. If you feel the stone in the passage, hasten to cut it open immediately, for if it does not come out at once, do not attempt to push your left index finger into him with oil if he is a boy or middle finger.
If the boy is fully grown, insert your hand into his seat and search for the stone until you feel it under your finger. Move it slightly towards the neck of the bladder, then press on it with your finger and push it out towards the spot where you intend to cut.
And orders a servant to squeeze the bladder with his hand, and orders another servant to stretch out his right hand with the scissors towards above, and with his other hand he stretches the skin that is below the scissors towards the place where the incision will be made. Then you take the cutting knife which has this shape:
And cut between the anus and the scrotum, not in the middle but towards the left side of the testicle. The incision should be directly over the stone, with your finger pressing the bladder outward so that the outside of the incision is wide and the inside is narrow enough for the stone to exit.
But if it is large, perhaps pressing the finger in the bladder will squeeze out the stone at the incision without difficulty. Know that some stones have angles and projections which may make their exit difficult.
And some are smooth like pebbles and round, making their exit easy. But if any have angles or projections, increase the incision slightly. If it still does not come out this way, do not hesitate to grasp it with forceps whose tip is like a probe.
So that it grips the stone securely and does not escape. Or else insert a fine, bent instrument underneath it. If you cannot manage it this way, widen the incision slightly. If something obstructs your view with blood, cauterize it with nitrate of silver.
If there are more than one stone, first push the largest towards the mouth of the bladder, then make an incision on it. Then do the same for the smaller ones. If they are extremely large, it is not permissible to make a big incision because it exposes the patient to two dangers.
Either he dies or he suffers from eternal incontinence because the wound will never close. But try to push it until it comes out, or break it with forceps and remove it in pieces.
If you have finished treating the wound, apply plaster and bandage it tightly. Then make a poultice moistened with oil or wine or rosewater and cold water to cool the hot swelling. After that, let the patient lie on his back without removing the bandage for three days.
When the wound opens, rinse it with plenty of water and oil. Then treat it with the bee honey poultice and the leek paste until it heals. If inflammation, heat, swelling or similar occurs, such as blood freezing in the bladder preventing urine from being expelled, which can be recognized by blood appearing in the urine...
Insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains it will cause the bladder to decay and become infected. Then wash the wound with vinegar, water, and salt, and apply whatever treatment is appropriate until it heals.
It is necessary during all stages of treatment to bind the thighs together to secure the drugs placed on the wound. If the calculus is small and has entered the urethra and stuck there preventing urine from being expelled, treat it with what I describe before it reaches the scrotum.
I have often resorted to this treatment instead of incision, as I have tried it and it appears thus:
Take an iron forceps with sharp points attached to a stick. Then take a thread and tie it around the penis below the calculus to prevent it from returning to the bladder. Next, gently insert the forceps into the urethra until it reaches the calculus.
Rotate the forceps with your hand on the calculus gently until it pierces through to the other side. Then release your grip, and the remaining part of the calculus will crumble and come out with the urine, healing the patient.
But if this method is not feasible due to some hindrance, tie a thread below the calculus and another above it. Then make an incision on the calculus in the penis between the two threads, and remove it.
Then the ligature is released and the clotted blood that has accumulated in the wound is cleaned. The first ligature must be tied underneath the stone to prevent it from returning to the bladder, and the second ligature should be tied above it so that when the thread is untied after the stone's removal, the skin will return to its original position covering the wound.
Therefore, when tying the upper ligature, you should lift the skin upwards so that it returns to its original position and covers the wound as mentioned.
Chapter Sixty-One
In the Removal of Stones for Women
It is rare for women to have stones. If one of them has a stone, its treatment is difficult and many reasons prevent it, among which are: the woman may be a virgin, or you may not find a woman who allows herself to be examined by the physician.
If she is a virgin or from those protected [by laws of modesty], the third reason is that you may not find a woman skilled in this procedure, especially when it comes to manual work; and the fourth reason is that the location of the incision for women is far from the location of the stone, so an additional incision may be needed.
There is danger in this, for if necessity requires it, a skilled female physician should be taken, but they are rarely found. If not, then seek a virtuous male physician or arrange for a skilled midwife knowledgeable about women's matters or a woman who knows something of this craft to assist.
Bring her and command her to perform all that you order regarding the examination of the stone first, namely to look if the woman is a virgin. If she is, do not insert your finger into her vagina and search for the stone. If it is found and pressed beneath her finger
Then command her to make the incision on her. If she is not a virgin but has given birth, order the midwife to insert her finger into the woman's vagina and search for the stone after placing her left hand on the bladder and squeezing it well.
If she finds the stone, she should gently draw it away from the mouth of the bladder downwards as far as her strength allows until it reaches the root of the thigh. Then she should make an incision on her opposite to half of the vulva at the root of the thigh, whichever side is convenient and where she feels the stone.
And her finger does not leave the stone, chewing beneath it. Let the incision be small at first, then introduce the hook into that small incision. If she feels the stone, increase the size of the incision according to what you know [to be] sufficient for the stone's exit. Know that types of stones are many.
And they are small and large, smooth and rough, long and round, with branches. Know their kinds so that you may distinguish among them according to what you desire. If bleeding overwhelms you, sprinkle powdered ginger on the place and hold it there until the bleeding stops, then return to your work.

And tie it with forceps tightly but gently, leave it without returning to it and leave the stone alone. Perhaps the living thing will perish. Then treat the wound, until after days the intensity of bleeding subsides and the place becomes inflamed, then return to your work until the stone comes out.

Chapter Sixty-Three
On Fissures of the Gluteal Muscle and Their Treatment
Know that a fissure on this muscle is one of the gravest matters, leading to destruction in most cases. Therefore, we see leaving it alone and refraining from operating on it; however, I mention its treatment and types of tumors here.
I say that many tumors can occur in the bodies where there is a composition of anthrax, and this may happen due to various causes such as excessive heat collecting at the anthrax, or from an injury. The color of the tumor will be like the natural skin color without any fluid present.
The tumor may be hard, and it might be congested with a purple color without any sensation. It could also result from the dilation of blood vessels and their swelling, as mentioned earlier, or from the swelling of veins. If it is due to the swelling of arteries, then the tumor will disappear once pressed upon.
If the tumor disappears when pressed with your fingers, then it is not due to vein swelling. However, if no change occurs upon pressing with fingers, then it is likely caused by vein dilation and may cause pain in the muscle and other flesh tissues.
To perform the procedure, first incise the skin of the scrotum. Then carefully push the testis upwards and out of the white tunic (tunica albuginea), freeing it from its blood vessels. Tie off the blood vessels and cut the testis away from all sides if it has adhered to neighboring tissues.
It is not necessary to remove the testis completely and cut it. However, if there is any adhesion between the tunics or between the blood vessels, all adherent tissues should be carefully freed and removed with a round excision.
If the inflammation of flesh is at the point of adhesion, which is behind it, all of it should be cut off and the egg removed as previously mentioned. Once your work is done, wash the wound with wool dampened in rose oil and water, then treat it with other remedies until it heals.

The Fifty-Second Chapter
In treating a prolapsed vein.
This prolapse occurs due to a hernia appearing in the posterior wall of the abdomen near the navel, causing the intestine to protrude into one of the scrotum.
This hernia occurs either from a fissure of the peritoneum or from its extension. These two types occur due to many causes, such as a blow, a jump, a cough, lifting a heavy object, etc. Its indication, if it is from the extension of the peritoneum, is that it appears gradually over a long period.
However, it does not occur suddenly and the tumor appears flat towards its depth because the peritoneum compresses the intestine. Its indication, if from a fissure of the peritoneum, is that severe pain occurs suddenly from the beginning, and the tumor appears different in appearance under the skin nearby.
And this is due to the exit of the intestine from the peritoneum, and its fate outside it. Sometimes the mesentery also exits, in which case this type of hernia is called an 'intestinal-umbilical' hernia. It may also contain gas, or fecal matter may accumulate there leading to the patient's death.
Because it causes severe pain and gurgling, especially when pressed. However, the treatment for these types of diseases with iron is dangerous, so one should avoid it. The method of treatment is to order the patient to push the intestine back into its abdomen by hand if possible.
Then he lies on his back with his legs raised, and you stretch the skin above the scrotum. Then cut open the entire skin of the scrotum lengthwise, then insert probes into the wound according to what is needed to widen it.

Between the white peritoneum beneath the tunica vaginalis and the second peritoneum, release the adhesion behind the testicle. Then insert your right hand into the scrotal skin, and with your left hand stretch the white peritoneum upwards and elevate the testicle towards the incision.

Then intertwine the threads together in a cross-stitch pattern and tie them firmly to the peritoneum we mentioned beneath the skin, on both sides. Then also wrap the thread ends and bind them tightly so that nothing can reach the vessels that nourish it. So that it does not cause inflammation and becomes a second tie outside the first, at least two fingers away. After these ties, leave about the width of a finger from the peritoneum beneath the skin. Chapter Seventy-Seven
Regarding hernias that occur in the scrotum
A hernia may appear in the scrotum as mentioned, but it will not descend into the anus unless it is easy and returns at all times.
But if time has prolonged it, the gap in the scrotum may increase until the viscera and testicles descend into the scrotum, exposing that which was previously in the abdomen as we have mentioned. And this is because the peritoneum stretches out then relaxes and twists at its site, and its treatment is by cautery as I have already described its method.
And it can be treated with iron on this condition: the patient lies on his back before you, then cut the location of the inflamed hernia horizontally at a length of three fingers under the skin.
Until, when the white peritoneum is exposed, take a thread and place it on the emerging peritoneum and push it into the abdomen's depth, then sew up the two openings at the end of the thread with sutures and stick them together.

And cautery is better in this case because it is closer to the vessels.
Chapter Eighty-Six.
On Relaxation of the Penis Skin.
It often happens that the penis skin relaxes in some people without the inner flesh relaxing, making it ugly to look at. Therefore, whoever desires its treatment should lay the patient on his back.
And cut off all the relaxed skin from the thick skin, then bring together the lips [of the incision], and if you wish, first stitch the excess skin with three or four sutures to secure it, then cut between the sutures.
Then treat it like other surgical wounds until it heals and the sutures fall out,
Chapter Ninety-Six.
On Castration.
And castration is forbidden in our religion.
Therefore, it is not fitting for me to include this in my book except that I mention it for two reasons: firstly, so that this knowledge may be available to the physician if he is asked about it, and secondly, because we often need to castrate some animals for our benefit.
The castration of beasts such as sheep, goats, cats and the like is of two kinds: either by cutting or by breaking and severing. That which is done by cutting is performed by sitting the animal in hot water until its female parts relax, soften, and droop.
Then milk it with your hand until it dissolves and cannot be felt. As for castration by cutting and severing, one should grip the animal and squeeze its scrotum with the left hand, then tie off the cords and make a single cut on each testicle.
Until the testicles appear, cut them off after peeling them. Leave nothing on them except the thin layer of membrane that is on the vessels. This method of castration is better than that done by cutting.
For cutting may leave some female parts behind, causing the animal to desire copulation. Then treat the wound until it heals.
Chapter Seventy.
On treating hermaphrodites.
There are two kinds of hermaphroditism in men: one appears externally or within the scrotum between the testicles, resembling a woman's vulva with hair and from which urine may flow.
And in women there is one kind, appearing above the vulva on the mons pubis like a small penis protruding externally, or two like female parts. Treatment for these three kinds:
The two kinds in men and the one kind in women should have the excess flesh cut away until its trace disappears, then treated like other wounds until it heals. As for the second kind in men that passes urine from within the scrotum, there is no treatment for it nor hope of recovery.
Chapter Seventy-One.
On cutting the clitoris and excess flesh protruding from women's vulvas.
The clitoris may be larger than normal, becoming prominent and unsightly, or in some women it may extend like a penis and lead to sexual desire.
It is necessary to grasp the clitoris with your hand or forceps and cut it off, taking care not to cut too deeply into its root lest bleeding occur.
Then treat it with surgical treatment until it heals; but the newly grown flesh is flesh that grows in the mouth of the womb until it fills it.
And perhaps it may exit externally, like a hernia. Therefore some ancient authorities called it "the disease of the navel", and it is necessary to cut it off like the prepuce, and treat it until it heals.
Chapter Two-Seventy
In treating fractures.
Rupture is when a woman's vulva is not torn or only slightly torn, and this can either be natural at birth or acquired due to some cause. The acquired type can be from superfluous flesh that has grown.
Or it may be due to a thin or thick membrane, located either within the uterus, on its sides, above or below. It prevents sexual intercourse and pregnancy, as well as childbirth, and may also prevent menstruation. The diagnosis is made by examination from the midwife.
If the obstruction is visible and close, then if it is not visible, search for it with your fingers or a probe. If the obstruction is a thin membrane and close to the labia minora, quickly cut it open by placing your thumb on either side of the labia minora.
The woman lies on her back with her legs spread. She then stretches the labia minora forcefully until the thin membrane is torn open and the obstruction is opened. Then she takes some wool, soaks it in oil, and places it on the spot. The woman should have sexual intercourse every day to prevent the wound from sticking together again.
If the membrane is thick and dense, do not cut it with a wide scalpel like a leaf of almonds. If the obstruction is from superfluous flesh, attach forceps to it and cut it off. Have with you drugs that stop bleeding without cauterizing, such as gum arabic, henbane, and milk mixed with egg white.
Then use a wide brass tube to prevent the wound from closing quickly. Hold it in place for some days, then use dry cotton lint and treat it with other methods until it heals. If there is further flesh growth inside the uterus, do not cut it in this manner.
If it is not cancerous, then the cancerous tumor that occurs in the uterus should never be treated with iron.
The Thirty-Seventh Chapter
In treating hemorrhoids and warts, as well as red pimples that appear on the genitals of women
And hemorrhoids are a swelling of the veins until they bleed profusely continuously. When a hemorrhoid becomes prolapsed, it turns into a wart. We have mentioned its types and signs earlier.
And I say that hemorrhoids and warts, if they are inside the uterus and have not appeared externally, cannot be treated with iron. But those that appear at the mouth of the uterus can be treated.
It is necessary for a woman to enter a cold house, stretch the warts with a comb or rough cloth, and cut them off at their roots. Then she should apply one of the drugs that stops bleeding without causing inflammation.
Such as Quicklime, Silica, and Honey. Then she should raise her legs against the wall for a while before lowering them into cold water. If bleeding persists, sit her in a decoction of Rue seeds, pomegranate rinds, and fig leaves. Then take wheat flour, mix it with honey and vinegar.
And apply this mixture to her back. If bleeding stops, then stop applying it. Otherwise, continue applying it to the buttocks and breasts without restriction. Then take a piece of flaxseed, soak it in a decoction of thyme or coltsfoot leaves or fig leaves with fig syrup, and apply it to the affected area.
If the tumor subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals. As for red pimples, they resemble the heads of lice and have a rough appearance. Do not cut what appears from them as mentioned earlier in the case of warts. Treat them until they heal.
The Fortieth-Seventh Chapter
On retention of menses in the uterus.
There are many types of tumors that can occur in the uterus, such as cancer, calcified tumors, ulcers, fistulas, erosions, warts, hemorrhoids, fissures, and hot tumors. All these diseases and their types and symptoms have been mentioned earlier.
It is necessary to mention in this chapter the hot tumor that appears in the womb, if it is one of those tumors that accumulate over time. If its pain at the beginning is sharp with pulsation and inflammation and fever.
When it is seen red and touched, do not rush to its cauterization. Treat it with what helps maturation until these symptoms subside. Then, when the woman should sit on a chair with two seats and lean on her back.
She should gather her legs towards the lower abdomen, keep her thighs apart, place her arms under her knees, and tie them with a suitable band.
So the midwife sits on the right side and uses the instrument that opens the mouth of the uterus, whose picture will come later. It is necessary to estimate gently the depth of the woman's uterus beforehand so that what enters from the instrument does not exceed its depth.
If the instrument hurts her, then if it exceeds the depth, it is necessary to place folds on the lip of the cervix to prevent the whole instrument from entering the uterus. The loop that runs in the instrument should be from the upper side.
And you hold the instrument, while the assistant turns the loop until the cervix opens. If the plug appears and is touched by hand and found to be thin, it should be cut at its tip with a wide scalpel. When all the period has been expelled.
It is necessary that a soft wick dipped in rose oil or green olive oil with some wax be placed in the wound. The wick should remain outside the incision in the cervix, and clean wool soaked in water boiled with henbane should be applied from outside on the uterus and pubis.
Then treat it after two days with the ointment suitable for that until it heals.
And the uterus and wound can be washed by injecting water and honey, then with water boiled with onion or long-leafed mint. Then return to the ointment, if the plug is hidden inside the uterus.
It is necessary to refrain from treating it with iron; rather treat it with what has been mentioned in the division.
Chapter Seventy-Five
In teaching midwives how to treat living fetuses if they are born abnormally.
A midwife should first know the form of natural birth, one of its signs being when she feels pressed downwards and desires to take a breath, and she finds relief from her labor pains.
If the fetus comes out quickly, know that this birth is in the natural form, with its head emerging first and the umbilical cord attached to it or hanging from its buttocks. If you see these signs, do not press her belly so that the baby may come out quickly.
However, if it comes out head-first, the placenta will also come out with it and be cleaned away nicely. Any other position is abnormal and condemned because the baby may come out feet-first or its hands may emerge before its head.
Or it may come out with one hand or foot first, or head and one hand, or emerge bent, perhaps upside down or in some other condemned position. Therefore, the midwife should be skilled and careful in all these matters and avoid mistakes.
And I have specified each of these positions and how to deal with them so that you may understand and rely on them. If the baby comes out head-first in the normal position, but the woman is having difficulty delivering it and her strength has weakened, seat her on a chair and summon some women to assist her.
And anoint her uterus with cooked fenugreek and damp cotton. Then the midwife should insert a small scalpel between her fingers and cut the umbilical cord, or use her nail to do so until its moisture flows out. Then press the woman's belly until the baby descends.
If it does not descend, then inject the woman with fenugreek juice mixed with deer tallow. Then tell her to push and use the candytuft plant to make her sneeze while holding her mouth and nose closed. If one of the baby's hands emerges first, gently pull them back a little.
If entry is not possible, place the woman on a pulpit and raise her legs above it. Then shake the pulpit gently while she holds on tightly to prevent falling during the shaking. If the hands do not enter and the fetus does not emerge, cut them off and pull out the rest of the fetus.
Or tie her hands with a cloth and pull gently until the fetus comes out, coming out feet-first. If the fetus comes out feet-first, do not push its legs upwards but turn it slightly until it becomes smooth. Then take one of its legs and stretch it slightly.
When it reaches the thighs, instruct her to cough and apply pressure with the forceps. If it does not come out as described, gently turn back the fetus until it returns to its natural position. It will then come out smoothly. If it still refuses to come out despite all these efforts.
Take some spittle of a dog and spittle of colocynth, ointment of wax and gum arabic dissolved together. Grind them all in a mortar until they become fine. Then apply it to the woman's vulva and below her abdomen before immersing her in warm water up to her navel.
When you see that her lower part has softened, make for her a suppository of myrrh and insert it. After some time has passed, seat her on a chair, make her sneeze, block her mouth and nose, and gently squeeze the lower part of her abdomen. The fetus will then come out from there, coming out on its knees and hands.
If it comes out in this manner, gently insert your hands to help its exit. Then have the woman lie on her back and let her buttocks hang down while she is lying on a bed. She should then hold her hands together before gently squeezing above her abdomen. Then remove the pillows from under her legs so that her buttocks hang down. If the fetus does not come out, take both of her legs together and shake them vigorously. Then gently squeeze above her abdomen until the fetus moves upwards. Then the midwife should insert her hand and turn the fetus slightly to make it smooth.
And the woman's order is to be delivered until the fetus comes out, and the fetus came out resisting, attached to one of her hands. If she cannot return her hand, then make the woman sit and let her walk if she cannot walk, let her lie down.
He made her lie down and shook her legs strongly, then he used the linen cloth that was mentioned among the bandages. If the waters are broken, sit her up on a chair, then deal with returning the hand and aligning the fetus in its natural position, blow on the woman's face and order her to push until it comes out.
The fetus comes out on its back with hands outstretched and face towards the mother's back. The midwife should take hold of the baby's hand, turn it gently bit by bit until it stands upright. Then carry out what was mentioned earlier about applying the oil and bandages.
Then tell her to move slightly, if she does so, sit her up on the chair and instruct her to lean towards the right side. Then tell her to push and blow into her face with the bellows, then the fetus will come out upright on its side.
If it descended into the mouth of the womb like this with the placenta, cut the placenta with a needle until it is emptied of moisture. If it is stuck to the baby's face and neck, sever it from the source lest it suffocate and die. Then push the baby back inside so that it returns to its proper position.
Tell the woman to push several times until it comes out easily. Know that twins are often born, and sometimes even three or four survive, although this is rare. Five is against nature and none have ever survived.
Surround them with one placenta even if they are many, and they separate from each other by a partition attached to the source of each. They come out like a single fetus, or emerge abnormally as described.
If some are difficult to deliver and assume the shapes we mentioned that are not natural, treat them as described. Let the midwife be gentle, patient, and skilful in handling each case with whatever means necessary to ensure safety.
The fetus formations in the womb that are aborted can be one, two, three, four, five, six, seven or more than ten. I have witnessed a woman aborting seven and another fifteen; all were formed.
By the Grace of the All-Wise, this knowledge belongs to the midwife, so perhaps she may encounter such a case someday and deal with it appropriately.
Chapter Seventy-Six.
In the delivery of a dead fetus.
If the dead fetus does not come out despite the treatment mentioned earlier, and you are forced to intervene manually, first examine [the woman] if she is strong and free from any signs of danger. Then, have her lie down on a bed on her back.
And let her head be tilted downward and her legs elevated, with a helper adjusting or tying them on both sides to prevent the body from shifting during the extraction.
Then moisten the mouth of the womb with a wet sponge dipped in honey, myrrh, and linseed oil. The midwife should also wet her hand with these substances before inserting it gently into the womb to locate suitable places for applying forceps.
Look, if the fetus is presenting head-first, insert the forceps into its eyes, forehead, mouth, throat, or under its beard or buttocks, or in the areas near the ribs or under the armpits.
If the fetus is presenting feet-first, insert the forceps into the pubic area or the middle of the ribs. Hold the forceps with your right hand and wrap its curve around your left fingers. Insert your hand gently and apply the forceps to some of the mentioned places.
Continue until you reach an empty space, then insert another forceps opposite it or a third one if needed to ensure even traction and prevent tilting. Pull gently in a horizontal direction, not just straight but also move it from side to side.
When the fetus comes out like a cucumber through a bottleneck, ease the traction intermittently. If any part gets stuck, apply some oil to your fingers and insert them from that side to rotate the stuck part. Once some of the fetus has come out, move the forceps to other positions.
Raise it slightly and do this until the entire fetus emerges. If a hand comes out before the rest and cannot be pushed back due to its constriction, wrap a cloth around it and then pull it until all of it emerges.
Either at the wrist joint or at the elbow, and similarly you should do with the other hand and feet. If the fetus' head is large and there is pressure on it during delivery or if there is water collected in its head, then you should insert a hooked probe between the fingers.
And cut through the head with it to release the water or use the instrument called the 'Mashdak' whose image is shown along with other instruments in the following chapter.
Similarly, if the fetus has a large head, you should cut through the skull or break it with the 'Mashdak' as mentioned earlier, then remove the bones with forceps. If the head emerges but is constricted at the neck, cut until the fluid in the chest cavity settles.
If the chest joins at that point, if not, cut as much as possible. If the lower abdomen is warm or contains heat, you should cauterize it until fluid flows from it.
If the fetus is breech, its extraction and turning towards the mouth of the uterus are easy. If it becomes constricted at the abdomen or chest, then pull it with a cloth wrapped around your hand and cut through the abdomen or chest until their contents spill out.
After removing all the other parts and if the head returns and is obstructed, then the midwife should insert her left hand. If the mouth of the uterus is open, she should insert her hand into the cervix, seek out the head with her fingers, and pull it towards the mouth of the uterus using tweezers or two tweezers.
If the mouth of the uterus has joined due to a hot tumor and there is inflammation, do not be rough with it. Instead, use warm, moist compresses and apply poultices, then sit in warm water that softens and moisturizes.
As for if the fetus is lying on its side, if it can be turned then use what was mentioned regarding live fetuses. If not, cut and remove it. Do not leave any placenta inside at all. After completing your treatment, use what was mentioned about treating hot tumors in uteri.
If bleeding occurs, apply pressure to the water retention area and use other treatments. I once saw a woman who became pregnant but the fetus died inside her. Then she became pregnant again.
Then the other fetus also died. After a long time, she developed an abscess in her uterus which swelled and opened, discharging pus. I was called to treat her but despite prolonged treatment, the wound did not heal. Therefore, I applied some strong drawing ointment.
So a bone came out of the site, then after some days another one came out. I was amazed by this as the womb does not contain bones. I presumed they were from the dead fetus' skull and upon searching the wound, I found many small skull bones.
I continued this treatment until I removed many bones from her and the woman recovered well. She lived like that for some time with a small discharge from the site. This is the story I am presenting here.
For it contains knowledge and assistance to what a practicing physician aims to achieve by his hands in treatment.
Chapter Seventy-Seven.
This chapter contains illustrations of the instruments needed for fetal extraction.

And their shape should be like a finger, and their length one and a half cubits. In the middle of the branches there are two projections of the same wood, secured to them, with a length of half a cubit or slightly more, and a width of about two fingers or slightly more.
These are the ones that enter into the mouth of the uterus to open it when you use the hooks, illustration of another similar but lighter and thinner instrument:
It is made from ivory or ebony wood in the shape of forceps, except that it has two projections at its tip as you see. Each projection is about one cubit long and two fingers wide. If you wish to use it to open the uterus,
I seat the woman on a bed with her legs dangling, spread apart. Then I insert these two retractors into the mouth of the womb, and you grasp the end of the instrument between her thighs. Open your hand with the instrument as you would with forceps, to whatever degree you wish to open the womb.
